      <p><b>Germany</b> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i>Deutschland</i>), officially <b>Federal Republic of Germany</b> (<i>Bundesrepublik Deutschland</i><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[8]</a></sup>), is a country in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>. The country's full name is sometimes shortened to the <b>FRG</b> (or the <b>BRD</b>, in German). </p>
      <p>To the north of Germany are the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Seas</a>, and the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>. To the east of Germany are the countries of <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>. To the south of Germany are the countries of <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>. To the west of Germany are the countries of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>. The total area of Germany is 357,021 square kilometres (137,847 square miles). The large majority of Germany has warm summers and cold winters. In June 2013, Germany had a population of 80.6 million<sup id="cite_ref-population_estimate_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-population_estimate-13">[9]</a></sup> people, the largest in Europe (excluding <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[10]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, Germany is the second most popular country for <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">migration</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Before it was called Germany, it was called Germania. In the years A.D. 900 – 1806, Germany was part of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>. From 1949 to 1990, Germany was made up of two countries called the Federal Republic of Germany (inf. <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>) and the German Democratic Republic (inf. East Germany). During this time, the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> was divided into a west and an east part. On 13 August 1961, <a href="/wiki/German_Democratic_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="German Democratic Republic">East Germany</a> started building the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a> between the two parts of Berlin. West Germany was one of the countries that started the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[12]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=1" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: History">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Change section: History">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lucas_Cranach_(I)_workshop_-_Martin_Luther_(Uffizi).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Lucas_Cranach_%28I%29_workshop_-_Martin_Luther_%28Uffizi%29.jpg/130px-Lucas_Cranach_%28I%29_workshop_-_Martin_Luther_%28Uffizi%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="130" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Lucas_Cranach_%28I%29_workshop_-_Martin_Luther_%28Uffizi%29.jpg/195px-Lucas_Cranach_%28I%29_workshop_-_Martin_Luther_%28Uffizi%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Lucas_Cranach_%28I%29_workshop_-_Martin_Luther_%28Uffizi%29.jpg/260px-Lucas_Cranach_%28I%29_workshop_-_Martin_Luther_%28Uffizi%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="479" data-file-height="700"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lucas_Cranach_(I)_workshop_-_Martin_Luther_(Uffizi).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a>, (1483–1546) started the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Germany gained importance as the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> of the German Nation, which was the first <i>Reich</i> (this word means <i>empire</i>). It was started by <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> who became the first <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> in 800&nbsp;AD, and it lasted until 1806, the time of the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Second Reich was started with a treaty in 1871 in <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Versailles" title="Palace of Versailles">Versailles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-timetable_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timetable-18">[14]</a></sup> The biggest state in the new German Empire was <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>. The rulers were called <a href="/wiki/Kaiser" title="Kaiser">Kaisers</a> or "German Emperors", but they did not call themselves "Emperors <i>of</i> Germany". There were many smaller states in the Empire, but not <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>. Germany stayed an empire for 50 years. </p>
      <p>In 1866 Prussia won the war against <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> and their allies. During this time Prussia founded the <a href="/wiki/North_German_Confederation" title="North German Confederation">North German Confederation</a>. The treaty of <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Germany" title="Unification of Germany">unification of Germany</a> was made after Germany won the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a> with France in 1871. In <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, Germany joined <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, and again declared war on France.<sup id="cite_ref-timetable_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timetable-18">[14]</a></sup> The war became slow in the west and became <a href="/wiki/Trench_warfare" title="Trench warfare">trench warfare</a>. Many men were killed on both sides without winning or losing. In the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Eastern Front (World War I)">Eastern Front</a> the soldiers fought with the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> and won there after the Russians gave up. The war ended in 1918 because the Germans could not win in the west and gave up. Germany's emperor also had to give up his power.<sup id="cite_ref-timetable_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timetable-18">[14]</a></sup> France took <a href="/wiki/Alsace" title="Alsace">Alsace</a> from Germany and Poland got the <a href="/wiki/Danzig" class="mw-redirect" title="Danzig">Danzig</a> corridor. After a revolution, the Second Reich ended, and the <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a> began. </p>
      <p>After the war, there were a lot of problems with money in Germany because of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Peace Treaty of Versailles</a>, which made Germany pay for the costs of World War I and the worldwide <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Third Reich was <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>; it lasted 12 years, from 1933 to 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[16]</a></sup> It started after <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> became the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. On 23 March 1933, the <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_(institution)" title="Reichstag (institution)">Reichstag</a> (parliament) passed the Enabling Act, which let Hitler's government command the country without help from the Reichstag and the presidency. This gave him total control of the country and the government.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[17]</a></sup> Hitler, in effect, became a <a href="/wiki/Dictator" title="Dictator">dictator</a>. </p>
      <p>Hitler wanted to unify all Germans in one state and did this by <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">taking over</a> places where Germans lived, such as <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>; Hitler also wanted the land in Poland that Germany had owned before 1918, but Poland refused to give it to him. He then invaded Poland. This started <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> on 1 September 1939. In the beginning of the war, Germany was winning and even successfully invaded France. It managed to take over much of Europe. However, Germany attacked the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> in 1941 and after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk" title="Battle of Kursk">Battle of Kursk</a>, the German Eastern Front began a slow retreat until war's end. On 8 May 1945, Germany gave up after Berlin was captured, Hitler had killed himself a week earlier. Because of the war, Germany lost a lot of German land east of <a href="/wiki/Oder-Neisse_line" title="Oder-Neisse line">the Oder-Neiße line</a>, and for 45 years, Germany was split into West Germany and <a href="/wiki/German_Democratic_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="German Democratic Republic">East Germany</a>. Other events happened during the war in Nazi Germany, including <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>, the mass <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> of Jews and other peoples, for which some Nazis were punished in the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Trials" title="Nuremberg Trials">Nuremberg Trials</a>. </p>
      <p>In 1989 there was a process of <a href="/wiki/Reform" title="Reform">reforms</a> in East Germany, which lead to the opening of the Berlin Wall and to the end of socialist rule in Germany. These events are known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Wende" title="Wende">Wende</a></i> or the <i>Friedliche Revolution</i> (Peaceful Revolution) in Germany. After that, East Germany <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">joined</a> West Germany in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[18]</a></sup> The new Germany is a part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=2" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Politics">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Change section: Politics">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Germany" title="Politics of Germany">Politics of Germany</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:IMO_at_German_National_Maritime_Conference_(33760358581).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/IMO_at_German_National_Maritime_Conference_%2833760358581%29.jpg/250px-IMO_at_German_National_Maritime_Conference_%2833760358581%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/IMO_at_German_National_Maritime_Conference_%2833760358581%29.jpg/375px-IMO_at_German_National_Maritime_Conference_%2833760358581%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/IMO_at_German_National_Maritime_Conference_%2833760358581%29.jpg/500px-IMO_at_German_National_Maritime_Conference_%2833760358581%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3840" data-file-height="2160"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Political_System_of_Germany.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Political_System_of_Germany.svg/250px-Political_System_of_Germany.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Political_System_of_Germany.svg/375px-Political_System_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Political_System_of_Germany.svg/500px-Political_System_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="721" data-file-height="506"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_reichstag_CP.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Berlin_reichstag_CP.jpg/220px-Berlin_reichstag_CP.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Berlin_reichstag_CP.jpg/330px-Berlin_reichstag_CP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Berlin_reichstag_CP.jpg/440px-Berlin_reichstag_CP.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4368" data-file-height="2912"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_reichstag_CP.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Germany is a <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitutional</a> <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">federal</a> <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[20]</a></sup> Its political rules come from the 'constitution' called <i><a href="/wiki/Basic_Law_of_the_Federal_Republic_of_Germany" title="Basic Law of the Federal Republic of Germany">Basic Law</a></i> (<i>Grundgesetz</i>), written by West Germany in 1949. It has a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a>, and the parliament elects the head of government, the <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany" title="Chancellor of Germany">Federal Chancellor</a> (<i>Bundeskanzler</i>). The current Chancellor, Dr <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a>, is a woman who used to live in East Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The people of Germany vote for the parliament, called the <i><a href="/wiki/Bundestag" class="mw-redirect" title="Bundestag">Bundestag</a></i> (Federal Assembly), every four years.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[22]</a></sup> Government members of the 16 <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">States of Germany</a> (<i>Bundesländer</i>) work in the <i><a href="/wiki/Bundesrat_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bundesrat (Germany)">Bundesrat</a></i> (Federal Council). The <i>Bundesrat</i> can help make some laws.<sup id="cite_ref-de-book_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de-book-27">[23]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="font-size: 95%"> 
       <caption>
        Main office holders

         <td> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> is the <i><a href="/wiki/President_of_Germany" title="President of Germany">Bundespräsident</a></i> (Federal President). This person has no real powers but can order <a href="/wiki/Elections" class="mw-redirect" title="Elections">elections</a> for the Bundestag. The current president is <a href="/wiki/Frank-Walter_Steinmeier" title="Frank-Walter Steinmeier">Frank-Walter Steinmeier</a> (SPD). </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Courts_of_Germany" title="Courts of Germany">judiciary branch</a> (the part of German politics that deals with courts) has a <i><a href="/wiki/Federal_Constitutional_Court_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Constitutional Court of Germany">Bundesverfassungsgericht</a></i> (Federal Constitutional Court). It can stop any <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">act</a> by the law-makers or other leaders if they feel they go against Germany's constitution. </p>
      <p>The opposition parties are the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_%2790/The_Greens" title="Alliance '90/The Greens">Alliance '90/The Greens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Die_Linke" class="mw-redirect" title="Die Linke">Die Linke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Free_Democratic_Party_(Germany)" title="Free Democratic Party (Germany)">FDP</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Alternative_for_Germany" title="Alternative for Germany">AFD</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=3" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Geography">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Change section: Geography">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Deutschland_topo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Deutschland_topo.jpg/170px-Deutschland_topo.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Deutschland_topo.jpg/255px-Deutschland_topo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Deutschland_topo.jpg/340px-Deutschland_topo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2011" data-file-height="2654"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Deutschland_topo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Topographic map
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Germany is one of the largest countries in Europe. It stretches from the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> in the north to the high mountains of the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a> in the south. The highest point is the <a href="/wiki/Zugspitze" title="Zugspitze">Zugspitze</a> on the Austrian <a href="/wiki/Border" title="Border">border</a>, at 2,962 metres (9,718&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-de-book_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de-book-27">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Germany's northern part is very low and flat (lowest point: <a href="/wiki/Neuendorf-Sachsenbande" title="Neuendorf-Sachsenbande">Neuendorf-Sachsenbande</a> at −3.54&nbsp;m or −11.6&nbsp;ft). In the middle, there are low mountain ranges covered in large forests. Between these and the Alps, there is another plain created by <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">glaciers</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Ice_age" title="Ice age">ice ages</a>. </p>
      <p>Germany also contains parts of Europe's longest rivers, such as the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> (which makes up a part of Germany's western border, while <a href="/wiki/Oder_River" title="Oder River">Oder River</a> is on its eastern border), the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Elbe" title="Elbe">Elbe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-de-book_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de-book-27">[23]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="States">States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=4" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: States">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Change section: States">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">

      </div>

        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Germany_general_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Germany
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      <p>In these states there are 301 <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_German_districts" title="List of German districts">Kreise</a></i> (districts) and 114 independent cities, which do not belong to any district. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=5" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Economy">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Change section: Economy">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Germany has one of the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technologically</a> powerful <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economies</a>. Bringing West and East Germany together and making their economy work is still taking a long time and costing a lot of money.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[25]</a></sup> Germany is the largest economy in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[26]</a></sup> In September 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation rate</a> in Germany was 2.5%. The <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment rate</a> of Germany was 5.5% as of October 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Germany is one of the <a href="/wiki/G8" title="G8">G8</a> countries. The main industry area is the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruhr area">Ruhr area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[28]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=6" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: People">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Change section: People">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg/220px-Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg/330px-Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg/440px-Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2970" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Neuschwanstein_Castle" title="Neuschwanstein Castle">Neuschwanstein Castle</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In Germany live mostly <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a> and many <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethnic_minorities&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ethnic minorities (not yet started)">ethnic minorities</a>. There are at least seven million people from other countries living in Germany. Some have <a href="/wiki/Political_asylum" title="Political asylum">political asylum</a>, some are <a href="/wiki/Guest_worker" title="Guest worker">guest workers</a> (<i>Gastarbeiter</i>), and some are their families. Many people from poor or dangerous countries go to Germany for safety. Many others do not get permission to live in Germany. </p>
      <p>About 50,000 ethnic Danish people live in Schleswig-Holstein, in the north. About 60,000 <a href="/wiki/Sorbs" title="Sorbs">Sorbs</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" title="Slavic peoples">Slavic</a> people) live in Germany too, in <a href="/wiki/Saxony" title="Saxony">Saxony</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg" title="Brandenburg">Brandenburg</a>. About 12,000 people in Germany speak <a href="/wiki/Frisian" class="mw-redirect" title="Frisian">Frisian</a>; this language is the closest living language to English. In northern Germany, people outside towns speak <a href="/wiki/Low_Saxon" title="Low Saxon">Low Saxon</a>. </p>
      <p>Many people have come to Germany from <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (about 1.9 million <a href="/wiki/Turks_in_Germany" title="Turks in Germany">Turks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kurds" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurds">Kurds</a>). Other small groups of people in Germany are <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croats</a> (0.2 million), <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italians</a> (0.6 million), Greeks (0.4 million), Russians, and <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poles</a> (0.3 million). There are also some ethnic Germans who lived in the old Soviet Union (1.7 million), Poland (0.7 million), and <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> (0.3 million). These people have German <a href="/wiki/Passport" title="Passport">passports</a>, so they are not counted as foreigners. A lot of these people do not speak German at home.<sup id="cite_ref-de-book_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de-book-27">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Christianity is the biggest religion; <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestants</a> are 38% of the people (mostly in the north) and <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholics</a> are 34% of the people (mostly in the south).<sup id="cite_ref-de-book_27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de-book-27">[23]</a></sup> There are also many <a href="/wiki/Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>, while the other people (26.3%) are either not religious, or belong to smaller religious groups.<sup id="cite_ref-de-book_27-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de-book-27">[23]</a></sup> In the eastern regions, the former territory of the <a href="/wiki/GDR" class="mw-redirect" title="GDR">GDR</a> (known as the <i>DDR</i> in German), only one fifth of the population is religious. </p>
      <p>Germany has one of the world's highest levels of schooling, technology, and businesses. The number of young people who attend universities is now three times more than it was after the end of World War II, and the <a href="/wiki/Trade_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade school">trade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Technical_school" title="Technical school">technical schools</a> of Germany are some of the best in the world. German income is, on average, $25,000 a year, making Germany a highly middle class society. A large <a href="/wiki/Social_welfare" class="mw-redirect" title="Social welfare">social welfare</a> system gives people money when they are ill, unemployed, or similarly disadvantaged. Millions of Germans travel outside of their country each year. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Moving_to_Germany_for_safety">Moving to Germany for safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=7" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Moving to Germany for safety">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Change section: Moving to Germany for safety">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>In 2015 there were wrong reports in some African, <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, etc. media channels about what it's like to go to and live in Germany. False promises of money, easy living and easy jobs were made. Germany is a very densely populated country, and especially in cities the housing situation is difficult and rents are high. Already in 2014 there were 39,000 <a href="/wiki/Homelessness" title="Homelessness">homeless people</a> in Germany and 339,000 people without apartment.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[29]</a></sup> Here is a link to a German video report<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[30]</a></sup> from a German news magazine. The video is about refugees, who have been living in a sports gym in Berlin for over a year with no privacy. In the video people discuss amongst others why there are problems to find living space in containers. The containers are similar to those in <a href="/wiki/Zaatari_refugee_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Zaatari refugee camp">Zaatari refugee camp</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=8" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Religion">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Change section: Religion">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Colognecathedralatnight.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Colognecathedralatnight.JPG/170px-Colognecathedralatnight.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Colognecathedralatnight.JPG/255px-Colognecathedralatnight.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Colognecathedralatnight.JPG/340px-Colognecathedralatnight.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2240" data-file-height="2648"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Colognecathedralatnight.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Cathedral" title="Cologne Cathedral">Cologne Cathedral</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> river is a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Frauenkirche_interior_2008_001-Frauenkirche_interior_2008_009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Frauenkirche_interior_2008_001-Frauenkirche_interior_2008_009.jpg/220px-Frauenkirche_interior_2008_001-Frauenkirche_interior_2008_009.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Frauenkirche_interior_2008_001-Frauenkirche_interior_2008_009.jpg/330px-Frauenkirche_interior_2008_001-Frauenkirche_interior_2008_009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Frauenkirche_interior_2008_001-Frauenkirche_interior_2008_009.jpg/440px-Frauenkirche_interior_2008_001-Frauenkirche_interior_2008_009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3120" data-file-height="2400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Frauenkirche_interior_2008_001-Frauenkirche_interior_2008_009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Inside the Frauenkirche (Church of Our Lady) in <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Germany's constitution says that all people can believe in any religion they want to, and that no one is allowed to discriminate against somebody because of the person's religion. </p>
      <p>In ancient times Germany was largely <a href="/wiki/Germanic_paganism" title="Germanic paganism">pagan</a>. <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a> was the biggest religion in Germany up to the 15th century, but a major religious change called the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Reformation</a> changed this. In 1517, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> said that the Catholic Church used religion to make money. Luther started <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestantism</a>, which is as big as the Catholic religion in Germany today. Before World War II, about two-thirds of the German people were Protestant and one-thirds were Roman Catholic. In the north and northeast of Germany, there were a lot more Protestants than Catholics. Today, about two-thirds of German people (more than 55 million people) call themselves Christian, but most of them do not practice it. About half of them are Protestants and about half are Roman Catholics.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-35">[31]</a></sup> Most German Protestants are members of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_in_Germany" title="Evangelical Church in Germany">Evangelical Church in Germany</a>. The previous Pope, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Benedict XVI</a>, was born in Germany. </p>
      <p>Before World War II, about one percent of the country's people were <a href="/wiki/German_Jews" title="German Jews">German Jews</a>. Today, Germany has the fastest-growing group of <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> people in the world. Many of them are in Berlin. Ten thousand Jews have moved to Germany since the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a>; many came from countries that were in the Soviet Union. Schools teaching about the horrible things that happened when the Nazis were in power, as well as teaching against the ideas of the Nazis, has helped to make Germany very <a href="/wiki/Toleration" title="Toleration">tolerant</a> towards other people and cultures, and now many people move there from countries that may not be so tolerant. </p>
      <p>About three million <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> live in Germany, 3.7% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-35">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[32]</a></sup> The country also has a large <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheist</a> and agnostic population, and there are also large about O.6 million <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> follower and some small group of Jain, Buddhist and Zoroastrian communities. The 20th century has also seen a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Germanic_neopaganism&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Germanic neopaganism (not yet started)">neopagan</a> revival. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=9" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Culture">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Change section: Culture">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Germany has a long history of poets, thinkers, artists, and so on. There are 240 supported theaters, hundreds of orchestras, thousands of museums and over 25,000 <a href="/wiki/Library" title="Library">libraries</a> in Germany. Millions of tourists visit these attractions every year. Some of the greatest classical musicians including <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Johann Sebastian Bach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Ludwig van Beethoven</a> and possibly <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a> were German. Some of the most revered scientists today like <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a> are German. </p>
      <p>Germany has created a high level of gender equality, disability rights, and accepts homosexuality. <a href="/wiki/Gay_marriage" class="mw-redirect" title="Gay marriage">Gay marriage</a> has been legal in Germany since 2017. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Food">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Change section: Food">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Germany is known for its food. The food varies from region to region. For example, in the southern regions, such as <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a>, they share their type of food with <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>. Everywhere in Germany, meat is eaten as a sausage. Even though wine use is increasing, the national alcoholic drink is beer. The number of Germans who drink beer is one of the highest in the world. German restaurants are also rated the second-best, with <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> rated first place. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=11" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Sports">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Change section: Sports">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Signal_iduna_park_stadium_dortmund_6.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Signal_iduna_park_stadium_dortmund_6.jpg/260px-Signal_iduna_park_stadium_dortmund_6.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Signal_iduna_park_stadium_dortmund_6.jpg/390px-Signal_iduna_park_stadium_dortmund_6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Signal_iduna_park_stadium_dortmund_6.jpg/520px-Signal_iduna_park_stadium_dortmund_6.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4133" data-file-height="2755"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Signal_iduna_park_stadium_dortmund_6.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Signal_Iduna_Park" title="Signal Iduna Park">Signal Iduna Park</a> is the biggest <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> stadium in Germany.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Football (soccer) is the most popular sport in Germany. The <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">national team</a> has won the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> 4 times, and appears in the finals a lot. The top football league in Germany is <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a>. Also, the <a href="/wiki/German_Football_Association" title="German Football Association">German Football Association</a> (<i>Deutscher Fußball-Bund</i>) is the largest in the world. Some of the world's best <a href="/wiki/Footballer" title="Footballer">Footballers</a> came from Germany. These would include <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Klose" title="Miroslav Klose">Miroslav Klose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Kahn" title="Oliver Kahn">Oliver Kahn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerd_M%C3%BCller" title="Gerd Müller">Gerd Müller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Ballack" title="Michael Ballack">Michael Ballack</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bastian_Schweinsteiger" title="Bastian Schweinsteiger">Bastian Schweinsteiger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Beckenbauer" title="Franz Beckenbauer">Franz Beckenbauer</a>, and so on. Plus, many tournaments have taken place in Germany. The most recent was the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA Women's World Cup">2011 FIFA Women's World Cup</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Audi_Cup" title="Audi Cup">Audi Cup</a> takes place in Germany every year in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>. </p>
      <p>Germany is also known for its motor sports. The country has made companies like the <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Audi" title="Audi">Audi</a>, etc. Successful German racing drivers include <a href="/wiki/Michael_Schumacher" title="Michael Schumacher">Michael Schumacher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Vettel" title="Sebastian Vettel">Sebastian Vettel</a>. </p>
      <p>Successful <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> players have also come from Germany, including <a href="/wiki/Steffi_Graf" title="Steffi Graf">Steffi Graf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boris_Becker" title="Boris Becker">Boris Becker</a>. More recently, <a href="/wiki/Sabine_Lisicki" title="Sabine Lisicki">Sabine Lisicki</a> reached the Women's Singles final at Wimbledon in 2013. </p>
      <p>Lastly, Germany is one of the best countries in the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>. Germany is the third in the list of the most Olympic Games medals in history (mixed with <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> medals). The country finished first place in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Winter_Olympics" title="2006 Winter Olympics">2006 Winter Olympics</a>, and second in the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a>. Germany got fifth place in the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a>. </p>

         <li id="cite_note-a-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-a_1-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">In the recognized minority languages and the most spoken minority <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Languages of Germany (not yet started)">language of Germany</a>:

              <li><a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani</a>: <i lang="rom">Federalni Republika Jermaniya</i></li> 
              <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Frisian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="North Frisian language (not yet started)">North Frisian</a>: <i lang="frr">Bûnsrepublyk Dútslân</i></li> 
              <li><a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">Almanya Federal Cumhuriyeti</i></li>
             </ul>
            </dd>
           </dl> </span></li> 
         <li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-3">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">From 1952 to 1990, the <i>Deutschlandlied</i> was the national anthem but only the third verse was sung on official occasions. Since 1991, the third verse alone has been the national anthem.<sup id="cite_ref-PresidentsOffice_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PresidentsOffice-2">[1]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-aa-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-aa_4-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> is the sole constitutional capital and <i>de jure</i> seat of government, but the former provisional capital of the Federal Republic of Germany, <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a>, has the special title of "federal city" (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Bundesstadt</i></i>) and is the primary seat of six ministries; all government ministries have offices in both cities.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-5">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Low_German" class="mw-redirect" title="Low German">Low German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sorbian_languages" title="Sorbian languages">Sorbian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romany</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Frisian_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Frisian languages (not yet started)">Frisian</a> are recognised by the <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages</a></span> </li> 
        </ol>
